\hypertarget{abstract}{%
\section{Abstract}\label{abstract}}

IOI is the \textbf{open operating stack that turns intelligence into
bounded autonomous institutions}. It supplies the semantic, execution,
authority, state, evidence, collaboration, and economic protocols required
for software intelligences to pursue durable goals and act across digital or
physical systems while remaining inside explicit constitutions.

The stack has three layers. \textbf{IOI L0} makes one constitution-bound
institution safely distributable across governed compute, state, verification,
human, and embodied nodes close to its users, data, tools, and infrastructure.
\textbf{AIIP} makes selective, positive-surplus interoperation between
separately sovereign institutions contractible through typed terms, work,
evidence, and contribution exchange.
\textbf{IOI L1} offers explicitly
enrolled systems optional shared registry, rights, assurance, dispute,
settlement, and economic-finality services. Local operation remains useful
on its own; network participation adds reach and shared trust.

IOI composes locally canonical semantic world planes with constitution-bound
runtimes and permits explicit versioned mappings where federation creates
value. Each system binds the domain semantics appropriate to its profile;
shared ontologies make objects, relationships, events, claims, actions,
policies, and goals interoperable where federation requires it. Hypervisor
turns those semantics into governed agency; wallet.network or applicable
domain governance supplies scoped authority; Agentgres admits operational
truth; and cryptographic receipts bind consequential transitions to their
policy, evidence, and result. This is IOI's formulation of \textbf{Web4}:
Read + Write + Own + Act, under machine authority.

For enterprises, this composition creates a governed learning boundary rather
than another model wrapper. Foundation models remain replaceable cognition
suppliers; the institution retains the ontology, admitted memory, corrections,
private evaluations, policies, workflows, datasets, lineage, and rights-eligible
derived capability that make its intelligence particular. A versioned
\textbf{InstitutionalLearningBoundaryProfile} compiles source rights,
policy-bound views, model-route rights, custody, training eligibility,
retention, export, and revocation into one fail-closed system boundary. This
profile joins Hypervisor, Agentgres, Foundry, Private Workspace, Ontology/Data,
and model-neutral routing without becoming a new runtime, authority plane,
truth store, application, or privacy tier.

Same-system distribution is a primary use of the stack rather than a preliminary
replication trick. One system may place useful work across execution nodes,
verifiers, gateways, people, robots, drones, sensors, and local controllers under
one constitution, membership and authority model, operational truth, and
lifecycle. Logical work assignment, partition behavior, reassignment, failover,
replay, and duplicate-effect prevention remain governed even when no external
counterparty or public consensus exists. This native L0 and Embodied Runtime
coordination is not AIIP.

The Internet of Intelligence emerges where independently governed systems hold
complementary capabilities, data-derived evidence, authority, locality,
resources, demand, or verification capacity and can create more value through
a bounded exchange than through their best permitted standalone alternatives.
IOI makes that cooperation surplus contractible: systems negotiate one exact
terms root, lease only the required capabilities and resources, preserve
contribution and rights lineage, settle accepted value, and exit with permitted
state. Collective intelligence is voluntary accountable cooperation among
sovereign systems, rather than centralized custody or presumed federation.

This paper presents that target architecture and its security and economic
logic. It is the publishing synthesis for contributors, reviewers, and early
integrators. Subject-specific owner documents in \emph{docs/architecture}
remain authoritative for detailed contracts, terminology, implementation
status, and conformance; this paper is reconciled to those owners as the
system evolves.

\hypertarget{executive-summary}{%
\section{Executive Summary}\label{executive-summary}}

Intelligence becomes infrastructure when it can carry responsibility across
time: interpret a domain, pursue an objective, acquire bounded resources,
coordinate specialists, act through real systems, evaluate the result, and
repair its own approach. IOI provides the operating and protocol layer for
that transition. Its unit of value is accountable progress toward an outcome;
its unit of control is a constitution-bound act.

The resulting system class is the \textbf{bounded distributed autonomous
system} (bounded DAS): a durable institution implemented as a governed state
machine whose purpose, authority, membership, evidence rules, lifecycle, and
shutdown posture are explicit. A bounded DAS may operate on one node or many,
under single authority, replicated single authority, threshold authority, BFT
consensus, or external-chain finality. When its admitted transitions form a
cryptographically continuous chain---binding sequence, predecessor,
operation, admission proof, resulting state, and receipts---it is an
\textbf{intelligent blockchain}. Consensus, a native token, and public-chain
deployment are selectable profiles rather than prerequisites.

IOI gives these systems a coherent life cycle. Builders compose and evaluate
an \textbf{Autonomous System Package}; genesis binds one release to a new
stable system identity, constitution, initial deployment and finality
profiles, governing authority, and sequence-zero roots. The live system then
runs, improves, recovers, migrates, adopts releases, undergoes governed
succession, or dissolves through typed transitions. This separation makes software
reusable while keeping every institution's history and authority distinct.

Two planes make the institution useful. \textbf{Domain Ontologies}
provide its semantic world: canonical objects, relationships, events, claims,
actions, policies, and goals. \textbf{Hypervisor} provides its agency plane:
execution, context, memory, tools, authority, evidence, effects, replay, and
recovery. Hypervisor Type 3 virtualizes those autonomy primitives; Type 2
places them on ordinary workstations; Type 1 extends them into governed
appliances, clusters, and HypervisorOS environments. The ontology makes the
world legible, and Hypervisor makes action within that world governable.

The clearest enterprise expression of those planes is \textbf{enterprise-owned
learning}. Hypervisor controls where institutional learning material may travel
and how it may be used; Agentgres preserves admitted learning state and lineage;
Ontology gives it domain meaning; Foundry converts individually eligible
evidence into reusable capability; Private Workspace can enforce
custody-proven containment; and model-neutral routing keeps cognition supply
substitutable. The institution's durable advantage is therefore not a hidden
provider thread. It is the governed combination of context, corrections,
evaluations, recipes, memory, policy, workflows, datasets, and derived
capability that can survive a provider change.

The protocol actor is the \textbf{Worker}. A Worker combines a manifest,
identity, policies, capabilities, receipt obligations, evaluation evidence,
and economic posture with one or more cognition backends. Those backends may
be hosted models, local open-weight models, retrieval systems, deterministic
tools, verifier ensembles, or routed mixtures. The model supplies cognition;
the Worker supplies bounded agency and accountable participation. This
abstraction supports a \textbf{Mixture of Workers}: planners, executors,
verifiers, tools, and services composed into evidence-bearing labor graphs.

Within one bounded DAS, \textbf{same-system distributed work} binds those
logical roles to admitted member nodes through deployment, membership,
\textbf{RuntimeAssignment}, work/resource/authority leases, state watermarks,
and receipt obligations. This is useful scale-out in its own right: a warehouse
fleet, distributed enterprise operation, research mesh, service network, or
multi-site physical system can coordinate one governed mission without
pretending its components are sovereign counterparties. Separate constitutions,
operational truth, risk, assets, and credible exit mark the later AIIP boundary.

Consequential work crosses the \textbf{Determinism Boundary}. Hypervisor
canonicalizes the proposed act, resolves capability and authority, evaluates
versioned policy, controls the effect, and emits receipts binding request,
decision, evidence, and result. \textbf{Agentgres} records admitted operations,
object heads, state roots, invariants, projections, contributions, and restore
truth inside each sovereign domain. \textbf{wallet.network} or the applicable
domain-governance path supplies scoped authority. Together these components
implement \textbf{alignment security}: probabilistic intelligence remains
flexible while enforceable consequence becomes explicit, attributable,
revocable, recoverable, and challengeable.

GoalRuns, WorkRuns, AutomationRuns, HarnessInvocations, ContextCells, and
external handles retain their own phases and owners while sharing exact-head,
idempotent, append-only lifecycle and typed-child mechanics. Platform
operability is likewise operation-specific rather than one health light:
required-plane ambiguity fails closed, degraded work needs an explicit
operation-scoped contract, failure only narrows assurance, and unknown effects
remain reconciliation-required across restart, restore, reassignment, and
failover.

IOI applies the same architecture to individual and collective pursuit, but
collective pursuit is not the default and does not presume shared incentives.
An OutcomeRoom materializes only when specialization, parallel exploration,
independent verification, reusable negative information, shared fixed costs, or
access to non-centralizable data and authority creates expected value greater
than the room's additional latency, spend, disclosure, semantic-mapping,
verification, counterparty, dispute, and settlement burden. A
\textbf{GoalRun} is the bounded orient, plan, act, observe, verify, repair,
course-correct, and continue-or-close loop for one participant or subteam. A
durable \textbf{OutcomeRoom} coordinates a shared objective across GoalRuns
through participant leases, a work frontier, claims, resource and capability
offers, attempts, findings, verifier challenges, result admission, and
contribution lineage. A cross-party room binds an exact
\textbf{CollaborationTermsEnvelope} root covering consideration, rights,
obligations, contribution eligibility, risk, exit, and settlement. Each durable
room is itself a bounded DAS with its own
genesis, constitution, identity, active profiles, state, and receipt chain.
This gives open agent swarms and private collaborations an institutional
substrate when cooperation creates participant-level surplus, while keeping
admission and authority precise.

\textbf{AIIP} extends that pursuit across sovereign systems only when their
governed decisions accept the exchange. It carries typed discovery, terms
proposals and responses, participation, work, evidence, result, and contribution
objects while preserving the policies and identities of their originating
domains. Participants may seek payment, accepted-outcome rights, reciprocal
capability, licenses or royalties, portable reputation, reusable learning,
strategic value, or shared-risk reduction. The north-star network proof is a
participant-rational exchange: an independently governed party can negotiate or
decline terms, receive scoped leases, contribute and be evaluated, preserve
credit and challenge rights, receive its contracted benefit, and exit with a
permitted state bundle while the sponsor measurably improves on its best
eligible local alternative or obtains an otherwise unavailable outcome.
Repeated positive-surplus exchanges that measurably improve later routing,
assurance, distribution, contracting, or settlement---not connection or
message volume---are what can create an Internet of Intelligence.

The architecture is \textbf{fractal and edge-in}. Personal devices, customer
VPCs, hosted sessions, confidential runtimes, provider nodes, and embodied
fleets all use the same artifact, authority, state-transition, and receipt
semantics. One logical system can add admitted nodes for durability, failover,
read scaling, useful concurrent execution, verification, gateway/edge presence,
embodied mission participation, or consensus according to its declared profile.
Its logical work graph and physical topology meet at governed runtime
assignments rather than an ambient cluster scheduler. Local operational
finality remains close to the work. Explicit
network enrollment can add registry, rights, reputation, assurance, escrow,
dispute, settlement, ordering, or public-finality services without moving
active cognition or private operational state onto IOI L1.

The product family exposes this stack through complementary surfaces.
\textbf{Hypervisor} builds, runs, supervises, and evolves governed autonomous
work. \textbf{Hypervisor Foundry} packages workers, evaluations, data, models,
and simulation or training environments. \textbf{ioi.ai} provides the Goal
Space conductor for intent intake, persistent goal state, collaboration,
synthesis, policy, budget, and replay. \textbf{aiagent.xyz} publishes, evaluates,
licenses, initializes, and routes Workers and managed instances.
\textbf{sas.xyz} procures autonomous service outcomes and packaged delivery.
\textbf{decentralized.cloud}, \textbf{decentralized.trade}, and
\textbf{decentralized.exchange} contribute infrastructure and market-route
intelligence. Domain Ontologies, Data Recipes, and the Ontology Development
Kit let builders apply the substrate to practically any institutional domain.

The commercial model follows the architecture. \textbf{Open substrate. Paid
network.} Local and self-hosted systems can operate from open contracts and
bring their own models, clouds, tools, and authority. Managed products charge
for useful autonomous work, persistent operation, collaboration, support,
distribution, routing, private execution posture, and selected trust or value
movement. The \textbf{Verified Work Graph} compounds evidence of who
contributed what, under which authority and system configuration, at what cost
and quality, and with what accepted outcome. \textbf{Work Credits} express
managed-product usage and budget; independent open goals use separately funded
bounties, procurement caps, or ServiceOrders. Model capacity comes from
provider API and enterprise arrangements, permitted customer-supplied access,
aggregators, and open or self-hosted weights under explicit route rights.
Managed billing advances through an exact fixed-point
quote/hold/usage/overrun/debit/downward-adjustment chain, while disputes advance
through an explicitly selected rail and one exact value-unit binding. An
accounting entry does not prove money moved, and an admitted dispute allocation
does not prove adjudication, escrow execution, appeal finality, or settlement.
The open/self-hosted substrate includes the complete learning-boundary contract;
IOI monetizes managed operation, compliance policy packs, confidential compute,
custody evidence, support, and model-independence testing rather than charging
for the customer's right to retain its own institutional intelligence.

This design exposes three potential value loops rather than an automatic
funnel. The \textbf{L0 product
loop} earns revenue by helping people and organizations create and operate
bounded autonomous systems. The \textbf{network loop} earns revenue only when
sovereign systems purchase discovery, routing, assurance, availability,
rights, reputation, or dispute services. The optional \textbf{L1 economic
loop} captures value from selected public and economic commitments. Adoption
can begin and remain with a useful local institution. A system federates through
AIIP only where network discovery, semantic translation, specialized supply,
independent verification, or shared trust costs less than reproducing the
capability internally or negotiating bespoke integration. It adds L1 services
only where neutral trust further reduces risk or enables an otherwise
unavailable transaction.

The thesis is deliberately concrete: an open network of intelligence becomes
useful when shared protocols make complementary work cheaper, safer, or newly
possible relative to each participant's outside option. Composability alone is
not value. IOI's contribution is the end-to-end operating stack that makes
accepted outcomes, retained sovereignty, attributable contribution,
participant-rational allocation, recovery, and settlement native to the
autonomous system rather than an application-specific layer assembled after
deployment.

F.5 Commercial Model-Supply Boundary (Non-Normative Procurement Evidence)

\hypertarget{web4-thesis-and-scope}{%
\section{\texorpdfstring{\textbf{1. Web4 Thesis and
Scope}}{1. Web4 Thesis and Scope}}\label{web4-thesis-and-scope}}

Web4 extends the web primitive ladder from Read, Write, and Own to
\textbf{Act}. Act is bounded machine authority: delegated software power
that becomes canonical, authorized, policy-bound, attributable,
revocable, and challengeable when it crosses a consequential boundary.

The Web4 thesis is therefore a \textbf{machine-authority thesis}. Read
made information addressable. Write made publication interactive. Own
made value programmable. Act makes delegated authority executable. IOI
exists because an open network of intelligence can only become useful at
economic scale if executable authority is alignment-secure at the
boundary where intent becomes consequence. Its builder thesis is equally
direct: IOI is the open operating stack that turns intelligence into bounded
autonomous institutions. L0 makes one institution safely distributable across
governed compute, state, verification, human, and embodied nodes; Hypervisor is the
reference execution and control environment; locally canonical Domain
Ontologies with optional versioned federation are
the semantic world plane; machine authority is the security protocol;
Agentgres is the operational truth substrate; AIIP makes selective,
positive-surplus interoperation between sovereign systems contractible; and IOI
L1 is an optional shared-trust and economic-finality layer.

The scope is intentionally limited. A browser click, local inference
step, draft, or file read need not become an on-chain transaction. The
requirement is that any boundary touching ownership, credentials,
durable state, third-party rights, escrow, or settlement must become
\textbf{transaction-shaped}: canonicalized, authorized, policy-bound,
receipt-backed, recovery-classified, challengeable, and eligible for the
declared settlement path.

The stable unit of governance is the bounded act performed by a worker
under an authority envelope, not the model response that proposed it.
Model internals can change, model outputs can vary, and models can be
swapped. The protocol-visible actor is the \textbf{Worker}: a bounded
execution unit with identity, manifest, policies, capabilities, receipt
obligations, and settlement posture. This worker-as-actor framing is
what makes Mixture of Workers possible at runtime, and a MoW worker
economy possible at network scale: routed labor graphs in which
planners, executors, verifiers, tools, and services can be selected,
paid, benchmarked, and disputed as accountable contributors.

The IOI architecture is local-first and fractal. Local execution
preserves speed, privacy, and zero marginal network fees. Provider
sessions add elastic capacity and specialized execution. Explicitly connected
or secured systems may use \textbf{IOI L1} for escrow, public identity,
assurance/security, sparse commitments, and disputes. The
invariant across those planes is not global execution; it is consistent
artifact semantics at the consequential boundary. The same canonical
ActionRequest, policy hash, approval chain, capability scope, and
receipt obligations apply whether the workload runs on a personal
device, a customer VPC, a hosted provider, a hardware-confidential
runtime, a cTEE/private workspace, or the Cryptographic Operator Plane.

To facilitate seamless integration into existing developer, operator,
and hosted-workflow environments, the Hypervisor local domain is
organized as follows:

1. \textbf{Hypervisor Node:} The headless execution and operational-finality
domain. It hosts governed autonomous-system chains, manages local
interop, processes local module invocations, and resolves local
authority outcomes without consuming public L1 gas.

2. \textbf{Hypervisor Core and clients:} Core is the shared
product/runtime substrate whose execution owner is the daemon.
Hypervisor App, Hypervisor Web, and CLI/headless are first-class clients
over Core; TUI is an optional terminal presentation.

3. \textbf{Systems, Work, and focused applications:}
Systems is the stable contextual read model for admitted bounded
institutions. Work is the policy-filtered projection across durable goals,
collective rooms, automation activations, Sessions, WorkRuns, reviews, and
incidents. Focused applications---including Developer Workspace, Foundry,
Governance, Operations, Provenance, and Packages---operate their declared
facets over the same Core without taking ownership from daemon/domain truth.

4. \textbf{IOI Authority Gateway, adapter targets, and harness adapters:}
The compatibility profile for existing IDEs, browser surfaces, MCP tools,
terminals, VMs, and local OS surfaces. External coding agents and
terminal-first agent systems are modeled separately as
\textbf{Agent Harness Adapters}. Both categories are mediated through
Hypervisor proposals, gates, observations, and receipts rather than
inheriting execution authority.

This is an \textbf{edge-in topology}. Authority-bearing work starts
close to the user, project, provider, or compute venue; becomes
canonical inside a domain kernel; and reaches IOI L1 only when explicit
network enrollment selects a public trust service.

The reader should expect this paper to introduce the runtime
architecture (Section 2), state and memory (Section 3),
network/routing/work-graphs including MoW (Section 4), settlement and
consensus (Section 5), cryptography and private-execution evidence (Section 6),
identity and authority (Section 7), economics and arbitration (Section
8), security and evolution (Section 9), and protocol surfaces (Section
10). Schemas and examples --- policy-envelope rules, effect-boundary artifacts, session
artifacts, dispute schema --- are collected in Appendix A. Other
appendices cover canonical envelopes, the developer quickstart with
connector manifest, claims and non-claims, fail-closed verdict logic,
and references.

\hypertarget{from-shared-gradients-to-verifiable-labor}{%
\subsection{1.1 From Shared Gradients to Verifiable
Labor}\label{from-shared-gradients-to-verifiable-labor}}

IOI differs from federated-learning and 6G visions of the Internet of
Intelligence. Those architectures primarily optimize cooperative model
training, gradient sharing, and distributed inference across edge
devices. IOI instead uses the term for an open operating fabric in which
bounded intelligences can discover shared work, negotiate meaning,
receive scoped authority and resources, contribute across sovereign
domains, preserve attribution and challenge rights, and carry permitted
state away. Execution, authority, operational truth, and settlement
remain distinct even when the user experiences one Goal Space.

The protocol does not require participants to reveal weights, training
data, prompts, datasets, or proprietary reasoning traces. Intelligence
may remain privately produced and privately owned. What becomes
protocol-visible is the Worker: its manifest, authority scope, policy
boundary, evaluation evidence, execution receipts, and contribution
claims.

The shared economic resource is not model internals; it is contractible access
to complementary capability and accepted contribution. A participant can
retain custody of its models, data, memory, and authority while exposing a
bounded service, evidence result, local act, or verified output whose value can
be attributed under accepted terms. Participation is always optional. A
rational system declines unless its expected utility under accepted terms,
minus the utility of its best permitted outside option and the incremental
costs and risks introduced by cooperation, is positive.

This shifts the organizing unit of the network from shared gradients to
verifiable labor. IOI does not require cognition to become public. It
requires consequential work to become accountable.

\hypertarget{north-star-internet-of-intelligence-network-proof}{%
\subsection{1.2 North-Star Internet-of-Intelligence Network
Proof}\label{north-star-internet-of-intelligence-network-proof}}

The proof has two ordered stages. First, IOI must demonstrate both distributed
continuity and useful distributed work for \emph{one} logical constitution-bound
autonomous system across two failure domains. The continuity proof binds admitted
membership and roles, checkpoint/log catch-up, state-root verification, writer
epoch and old-writer fencing, controlled failover, replay, drain/removal, and
unchanged authority. The useful-work proof concurrently places bounded work on
multiple admitted execution or embodied nodes, preserves state and evidence
watermarks, reassigns expired or failed claims, prevents duplicate consequential
effects, uses independent verifier roles where selected, and reconciles
partitions and rejoin. Two processes or replicas do not yet prove independent
governance, consensus, or a network, but one system coordinating useful work
across them is a primary L0 product capability rather than merely seed behavior.

Second, IOI has demonstrated an Internet of Intelligence only when an independently
operated external Worker can discover eligible work through a versioned,
policy-bound OutcomeRoom discovery projection; negotiate or decline an exact
collaboration terms root plus semantic and action profiles; submit a typed
participation request; receive bounded context,
resource, capability, authority, and budget leases; claim work; return a
verifiable contribution; preserve credit and dispute lineage; and exit with a
portable permitted participant-state bundle. The proof must not require one
runtime, operational database, administrator, or continued access to or trust
in an IOI-hosted room.

The proof must also be economically non-theatrical. The external principal
voluntarily accepts disclosed cost, rights, privacy, verification, dispute, and
reward terms; the sponsor obtains a measurable improvement over its best
eligible local alternative or an otherwise unavailable outcome; and the
participant receives its declared payment, outcome right, reciprocal access,
reputation, reusable state, or other benefit. Independent operation without
participant-level value proves interoperability, not a network economy.

Same-owner multi-model, multi-worker, or multi-node orchestration is a primary
same-system distributed-work proof, but it is not this cross-system network
proof. Neither a large IOI-operated
fleet nor a visually busy collaboration surface establishes federation by
itself. The decisive property of the second stage is an independently governed principal entering,
contributing, being verified and attributed under declared terms, and leaving
without surrendering sovereignty.

\hypertarget{the-ioi-runtime-architecture}{%
\section{2. The IOI Runtime
Architecture}\label{the-ioi-runtime-architecture}}

IOI is defined by a \textbf{fractal, edge-in operating fabric}. Work
begins near users, data, tools, providers, and physical systems. The
\textbf{Hypervisor Node} is the local execution, orchestration, replay,
interop, and settlement domain. Inside it, the \textbf{Hypervisor
Daemon} owns execution semantics and gates consequential effects;
wallet.network or the applicable local/domain governance path authorizes
power; Agentgres admits operational truth. Domain Ontologies
make semantic objects and actions interoperable without creating a
globally mutable database, and AIIP carries voluntarily accepted, terms-bound
work and evidence between sovereign domains.

Rather than running as ad-hoc scripts, autonomous systems run as
\textbf{Governed Autonomous-System Chains}. These are system-local, logically
scoped stateful
constitution-bound state machines containing policies, modules, proposals,
ordered operations, lifecycle rules, and receipts, compiled and run strictly under the Hypervisor Daemon or
daemon-mediated domain APIs. Scoped execution paths remain owner-qualified:
agent steps resolve through a selected HarnessProfile or
AgentHarnessAdapter; deterministic and service steps through a ServiceModule
and ModuleInvocation; tool or connector effects through a
RuntimeToolContract; cognition through a model route; acceptance through a
VerifierPath; and cross-system work through an AIIP handoff. The Default
Harness Profile is one reference HarnessProfile, not an umbrella for those
other paths. Hypervisor Core coordinates selection and session state; the
daemon/domain gate owns consequential execution. The
Hypervisor Node manages local interop and settles authority outcomes
through Agentgres. Explicitly enrolled systems may anchor selected roots to IOI
L1 only when a chosen registry, assurance/security, economics, reputation, or
dispute service requires it.

An \textbf{intelligent blockchain} is the ordered state-machine embodiment of
such a bounded autonomous institution. It need not be a public chain, use a
native token, or run multi-node consensus. Single-authority/PoA-1, replicated
single authority, threshold authority, BFT consensus, and external-chain
finality are declared profiles. Intelligence may propose and evaluate changes;
the active constitution, policy, authority, ordering, oracle/evidence, effect,
and receipt gates decide what becomes canonical. The classification requires
cryptographic continuity under every profile: each admitted operation or batch
binds a monotonic sequence, expected predecessor commitment, operation/batch
commitment, admission proof, resulting state root, and receipt root. A bounded
autonomous application without that commitment chain is not called a
blockchain.

ioi.ai's reusable \textbf{OutcomeRoom} package is the first flagship/reference
bounded-DAS profile because it exercises agent ingress, workgraphs,
verification, contribution lineage, and course correction. Each durable room
genesis creates a distinct bounded DAS with its own stable system identity,
constitution, active profiles, and cryptographic admission spine; the hosted
service operates many such systems. OutcomeRoom is not the definition of L0;
enterprise operations, asset or treasury mandates, research institutions,
service networks, embodied fleets, and other ontologies use the same substrate
without inheriting a room or swarm UI.

\textbf{Autonomous System Package.} Hypervisor's primary developer
artifact is the \emph{Autonomous System Package}: the reusable release object
that versions and distributes typed \textbf{GoalRunProfile},
\textbf{WorkflowTemplate}, \textbf{AutomationSpec}, \textbf{HarnessProfile},
\textbf{AgentHarnessAdapter}, \textbf{SkillManifest}, \textbf{DataRecipe},
\textbf{RuntimeToolContract}, immutable MCP gateway
requirement, worker, model, authority-requirement,
memory/state/artifact, evaluation, constitution/profile-template, and receipt
components without taking over their canonical ownership. It is not a raw
workflow file, connector config, daemon process, UI canvas, live system identity,
membership, or enrollment. Package and live-system lifecycles are separate:
Every immutable component is pinned by exact revision and content hash in a
component-set snapshot committed by the release root. SkillEntry,
AutomationInstallationBinding, live MCP gateway profile, ContextLease,
RuntimeAssignment, authority grant, endpoint, readiness, and run state remain
outside the Package.

\begin{center}
\emph{package: compose -> bind requirements -> simulate/evaluate -> package ->
sign -> release -> promote -> deprecate or revoke}

\emph{system: instantiate/genesis -> authorize -> activate -> run -> improve ->
recover, migrate, fork, adopt, succeed, dissolve, retire, archive, or decommission}
\end{center}

The \textbf{AutonomousSystemGenesisEnvelope} alone binds one selected package
release to a new \emph{system://} identity, active constitution and initial
profiles, governing decision and authority, sequence-zero operation/transition
commitment, and initial state and receipt roots. An existing system adopts a
later release through governed upgrade; it does not create another genesis or
change identity.

The Workflow Compositor shapes immutable, versioned WorkflowTemplates for
high-level directed workflow/service graphs and step contracts that may mature
into an Autonomous System Package. Selected HarnessProfiles, service modules,
model mounts, connectors, verifiers, and AIIP/capability exits resolve scoped
steps under daemon gates.

This architecture serves as a governed improvement sandbox. Autonomous
systems may inspect traces, identify failure modes, extract skills, and
draft upgrade proposals, but they do not self-modify directly. Accepted
changes enter the system only through daemon-mediated operations,
Agentgres admission, policy gates, receipts, and, for high-assurance
deployments, continuity proofs that bind the new generation to the same
or narrower authority envelope.

Ordinary improvement cannot amend protected purpose, prohibitions, authority or
effect ceilings, amendment gates, ordering/finality, oracle policy, emergency
stop, succession, dissolution, or decommission through the same path as a skill
or workflow patch. Self-preservation, replication, resource acquisition, and
code propagation remain subordinate to the constitution, governed membership,
external revocation, and terminal shutdown.

This stack is designed to be fractally self-similar at its execution and
domain boundaries: reusable contracts operate on user devices, provider
Sessions, customer infrastructure, and sovereign domains. Those
environments differ in capacity and trust profile, but share artifact
semantics, canonical payloads, binding hashes, and evidence rules, so
outcomes can move across Hypervisor Sessions, provider environments, MoW
routes, and service-outcome contracts without reinterpretation. IOI L1
does not run the Hypervisor runtime or active cognition; it receives only
selected roots and commitments whose rights, registry, reputation,
economics, governance, or dispute semantics require shared finality.

\hypertarget{the-protocol-core-the-four-pillars-of-agency}{%
\subsection{2.1 The Protocol Core: The Four Pillars of
Agency}\label{the-protocol-core-the-four-pillars-of-agency}}

To make probabilistic AI accountable at declared effect boundaries---and to
make Own executable as Act---the IOI runtime relies on four coupled contract
families. They bound consequential effects admitted through covered control
points; they do not imply interception of every thought, tool, opaque process,
or external mutation:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Pillar 1: Canonicalization.} A covered consequential request is
  normalized into its declared canonical representation before hashing. This
  provides byte-level stability for that request profile; unmediated behavior
  remains outside the claim.
\item
  \textbf{Pillar 2: Policy Binding (policy\_hash).} The selected rule
  representation, precedence, and decision procedure are deterministic and
  version-bound. Observation inputs such as focus, DOM state, visual targets,
  or provider reports retain their declared heuristic, freshness, and assurance
  limits. The \emph{policy\_hash} binds the policy version used for one decision;
  governed policy transitions remain possible.
\item
  \textbf{Pillar 3: Pre-Effect Commitment:} Before a covered side-effect
  crosses its mediated host, provider, connector, browser, or tool boundary, the runtime
  binds the request hash, the policy hash, and any required user
  approvals (binding the exact request hash, scope, expiry, and
  revocation epoch) into the transaction-shaped evidence bundle for the
  act.
\item
  \textbf{Pillar 4: Evidence and Settlement Binding.} Applicable receipts
  bind the request, policy, authority decision, result, and evidence refs.
  When a declared trigger requires public or economic finality, a settlement
  profile may commit selected receipt or evidence roots to escrow, rights,
  dispute, or payout contracts. This makes the declared boundary auditable;
  it does not by itself prove legal liability or every real-world fact.
\end{enumerate}

Design Doctrine: Process Safety over Model Safety

IOI accepts that global consensus is too slow for cognition and local
execution is too unsafe for settlement. Furthermore, attempting to force
bit-for-bit determinism onto the neural network inference layer
fundamentally breaks the utility of modern AI.

IOI achieves verifiable agency by moving safety invariants out of the
"black box" of the model and into explicit, checkable protocol surfaces
at the execution boundary:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Canonicalization \& Pinned IO:} Makes the declared decision and
  evidence boundary auditable even when inference is stochastic. Each effect
  declares whether it is replayable, checkpointable, compensatable,
  reconciliation-required, or non-retryable; the protocol never infers
  real-world reversibility from a reproducible request.
\item
  \textbf{Typed Intent, Steps, and Acceptance:} Enforces hard
  constraints and strict type-matching before any model-based judgment
  is permitted to cross into shared reality.
\item
  \textbf{Governed Remediation and Failure Routing:} Acknowledges that
  agents will fail. A repair opens a new ActionProposal, gate, admitted
  effect, and receipt set rather than silently mutating or retrying the
  original effect.
\item
  \textbf{Content-Addressed Evidence \& Due Process:} Narrows disputes by
  distinguishing receipts and committed evidence from observational events
  and analytics. Receipts prove only the fields, bindings, and verifier claims
  covered by their profile; events observe and analytics improve. Contractual,
  semantic, physical, and legal questions may still require declared
  verifiers, adjudication, or human review.
\end{itemize}

\hypertarget{the-hypervisor-daemon-multi-plane-architecture}{%
\subsection{2.2 The Hypervisor Daemon \& Multi-Plane
Architecture}\label{the-hypervisor-daemon-multi-plane-architecture}}

The \textbf{Hypervisor Daemon} is the canonical execution-semantics and
effect-admission owner for daemon-managed work and the declared control points
of mediated adapter lanes.
It is not the settlement ledger, not the raw L0 consensus engine, and
not the client SDK; it is the host runtime that enforces the
deterministic boundary. Fully managed runtime nodes initialize a compatible
daemon runtime-node profile. Direct cloud, SSH, storage, connector, hosted
harness, and other adapter lanes preserve their real semantics and mediate the
control points they can observe; they do not claim total interception of an
opaque third-party runtime.

Hypervisor Node Local Boundary:

-- The \textbf{Hypervisor Daemon} manages local execution,
containerization, and tool call intercept normalization.

-- \textbf{Hypervisor App}, \textbf{Hypervisor Web}, and
\textbf{CLI/headless} expose client lenses over the same Core. Developer Workspace,
Foundry, provider/environment views, approvals, receipts, logs, replay,
and restore controls are projections over daemon and Agentgres truth.

-- \textbf{Agentgres} maintains the local operational truth log
(accepted actions, object states, projections, and receipt chains).

-- \emph{wallet.network} operates as the local authority plane, managing
secrets, step-up prompts, and temporary cryptographic execution grants.

-- \textbf{Agent Wiki / ioi-memory} handles semantic vector indexing and
retrieval. Note that authoritative memory mutations are not written
directly to memory blocks; they must be admitted into Agentgres via
operation-backed commits.

Hypervisor Core exposes implementable work, session, and adapter objects rather
than hiding environment operations behind product screens. A
\textbf{HypervisorProject} binds stable build/workspace identity, default
policies, persistence defaults, adapter preferences, and Agentgres domain
links. An \textbf{AutomationSpec} is reusable standing behavior; an
immutable successor-versioned \textbf{AutomationInstallationBinding} owns
owner- or System-scope enablement and narrowing policy overlays; an
\textbf{AutomationRun} freezes both plus the exact WorkflowTemplate for one
activation. A \textbf{GoalRun} is durable
bounded outcome pursuit, an \textbf{OutcomeRoom} is persistent collective
pursuit, a \textbf{HypervisorSession} is a bounded interactive, headless, or
supervisory execution/control context, and a \textbf{WorkRun} is one admitted
execution. Background is an execution mode, not a canonical object kind.
Mission may remain optional product language backed by exactly one GoalRun or
OutcomeRoom, but it creates no independent identity, lifecycle, budget,
authority, state, evidence, or receipts.

Sessions are bounded execution units; they do not replace durable goal or room
identity. Environments are managed resources behind sessions, providers are
cross-session resources, and a
\textbf{RuntimeAssignment} / placement decision binds a GoalRun, role, Context
Cell, work claim, typed work subject, or embodied unit to its owning \emph{system\_id},
active deployment profile, admitted node membership and role lease, runtime/environment and
compute session, required state watermark and locality, authority/evidence
posture, partition/reassignment and duplicate-effect policy, reconciliation
path, and receipt obligations. An embodied placement additionally binds the
unit and controller, and a distributed multi-unit or multi-membership mission
binds its current fleet-allocation lease. A fleet-of-one needs no allocation
record merely to exist or run. This is a native L0 operation, not AIIP. No
one-session/one-VM relationship is
required: a session may use a local workspace, VM, microVM, browser sandbox,
hosted worker, HypervisorOS node, customer boundary, or another declared
environment class.

\textbf{AdapterConnectionProfile} declares how a session connects to an
editor, terminal, browser, VM, container, local OS surface, hosted
worker, HypervisorOS node, or external harness. A
\textbf{HypervisorHarnessSelectionOption} selects either a
HarnessProfile or an exact \textbf{AgentHarnessAdapter} revision/hash. External harnesses
emit \textbf{HarnessAdapterReceipt} envelopes; containerized harness lanes are
planned with \textbf{HarnessContainerLanePlan} and closed with
\textbf{HarnessContainerLaneReceipt}. These objects let Codex-like,
Claude-Code-like, Grok-Build-like, OpenHands-like, Aider-like, or
DeepSeek-TUI-like harnesses propose work through daemon gates without
becoming Hypervisor clients or runtime truth.

Managed environments use \textbf{HypervisorEnvironmentClass},
\textbf{HypervisorEnvironmentOpsProfile},
\textbf{HypervisorEnvironmentLifecycleState},
\textbf{HypervisorEnvironmentActivitySignal},
\textbf{HypervisorEnvironmentService},
\textbf{HypervisorEnvironmentTask},
\textbf{HypervisorEnvironmentPort}, and
\textbf{HypervisorScmAuthRequirement}. Access to editors, SSH, browser
previews, logs, support bundles, port shares, SCM actions, task exec,
and environment operations is governed by a
\textbf{HypervisorSessionAccessLease}; any \textbf{SessionAccessToken}
is derived token material under that lease. \textbf{PortExposurePolicy},
\textbf{BrowserOpenPolicy}, and \textbf{SupportBundlePolicy} define what
may be opened, proxied, shared, recorded, or exported. These are
daemon/Core contracts and Agentgres projections, not UI-only controls.

This segregation reduces credential and filesystem exposure and makes admitted
crossings transaction-shaped. It does not make opaque worker behavior or
unobserved external effects transaction-shaped by implication.

The \textbf{Hypervisor Daemon} holds exclusive ownership over execution
semantics, tool boundaries, effect admission, runtime state transitions,
lease lifetimes, receipt generation, the emission and normalization of
execution traces and trace refs, and state commitments to Agentgres
(replay and reconstructability are grounded in Agentgres operations,
receipts, and artifact refs). Rather than hosting an independent,
parallel runtime engine, the daemon mediates \textbf{HarnessProfiles}.
The \textbf{Default Harness Profile} is the IOI reference scaffold and
fallback for loop-native scoped step resolution. It is useful for
custom service steps, single-worker loops, and local development, but it
is not a global meta-harness and not the owner of high-level workflow
composition. Third-party agent harnesses, service modules, model
mounts, verifiers, AIIP peers, and Rust/WASM workload paths participate
through common boundary objects, adapter conformance, and daemon gates.

\textbf{Rust/WASM step-module backend.} IOI's target execution shape routes
consequential daemon steps through the Rust/WASM workload/kernel
substrate as the authoritative step/module execution backend under the
daemon. A serious step should materialize as a
\textbf{StepModuleInvocation} with authority refs, context refs,
artifact refs, state-root expectations, and receipt obligations, and
close as a \textbf{StepModuleResult} or normalized observation admitted
through Agentgres. This substrate is not a peer runtime beside
Hypervisor; it is the canonical backend behind daemon-mediated
execution.

Product clients and adapter surfaces may enter through daemon routes for
HTTP clients, UI state, local adapter coordination, and existing Hypervisor
surfaces. Canonicality is determined by typed envelopes, authority
checks, receipts, state roots, and Agentgres admission rather than by the
client implementation. The canonical execution sequence is:
\textbf{ActionProposal} to \textbf{GateResult} to
\textbf{StepModuleInvocation} through a typed daemon-core API or
Rust/WASM workload client, then \textbf{StepModuleResult},
\textbf{NormalizedObservation}, receipt refs, state-root updates, and
Agentgres admission. Implementations may use different transports only
when they preserve these protocol envelopes and evidence obligations.

Execution is strictly bifurcated between two cooperating layers:

-- The \textbf{Probabilistic Cognitive Plane (Model Loop)} interprets
context, plans actions, adapts to exceptions, requests semantic
evidence, handles domain ambiguity, and proposes state deltas.

-- The \textbf{Deterministic Safety Plane (Hypervisor Daemon)} enforces
hard limits, validates inputs, records execution traces, manages
credential scopes, schedules execution segments, emits cryptographic
receipts, and commits admitted state transitions to Agentgres.

\textbf{The Loop-Native Execution Cycle.} Every governed autonomous task
uses loop-native semantics where adaptation is needed: model or harness
pass, action proposal, policy/authority gate, execution, result
normalization, receipt and Agentgres update, and model or harness
re-entry. Higher-level directed workflow/service shape belongs to the
Workflow Compositor; lower-level step resolution belongs to the selected
HarnessProfile or module path. All consequential transitions must cross
the determinism boundary through normalized IO interfaces. Consequential
steps are executed as typed Service Module Invocations, direct daemon
tools, model/inference mount calls, cTEE/private workspace actions,
verifiers, or AIIP/capability exits, and the daemon writes governed
transitions and state-transition commitment records through Agentgres-compatible
APIs without writing directly to IOI L1.

The loop continues iteratively until the task achieves resolution, at
which point the final cognitive output must undergo an explicit
\textbf{Output Ownership Pass}. This pass verifies that the final
delivery is fully accounted for by cryptographic evidence, local
observations, receipts, and valid Agentgres artifact references before
the task can be marked complete and authorized for L1 settlement or
local master integration.

\textbf{Canonical loop (determinism boundary shown):}


\begin{center}
\needspace{6\baselineskip}
\begin{tikzpicture}[scale=1,transform shape,node distance=5mm and 10mm]
\node[font=\sffamily\footnotesize\itshape] (cl) {PROBABILISTIC COGNITIVE PLANE (Model Loop)};
\node[ioiplain,below=2mm of cl,text width=60mm] (mp){Model Pass};
\node[ioiplain,below=of mp,text width=60mm] (ap){Action Proposal};
\draw[ioiflow](mp)--(ap);
\draw[ioiflow](ap) to[bend left=55] node[ioilabel,left]{iterate} (mp);
\node[draw,fill=ioikw!12,rounded corners,below=8mm of ap,text width=74mm,align=center,font=\sffamily\footnotesize] (b){Crosses the Determinism Boundary\\(canonical \texttt{ActionRequest})};
\node[ioibox,below=5mm of b,text width=74mm] (pg){Policy Gate \footnotesize(policy\_hash + scope)};
\node[ioibox,below=of pg,text width=74mm] (ex){Bounded Execution};
\node[ioibox,below=of ex,text width=74mm] (rc){Receipt Commitment};
\node[ioiplain,below=of rc,text width=74mm] (st){Authorized Settlement};
\node[font=\sffamily\footnotesize\itshape,below=2mm of st] {DETERMINISTIC SAFETY PLANE};
\draw[ioiflow](ap)--(b);\draw[ioiflow](b)--(pg);\draw[ioiflow](pg)--(ex);\draw[ioiflow](ex)--(rc);\draw[ioiflow](rc)--(st);
\end{tikzpicture}
\end{center}

\textbf{Product domains are not runtime nodes by default.} A web app,
marketplace, or product surface may create runtime assignments, request
daemon-compatible execution, or project runtime state, but workers
execute inside local, hosted, decentralized, enterprise, TEE, or
customer-boundary runtime profiles.

A \textbf{managed worker instance} does not make aiagent.xyz the
execution runtime. aiagent.xyz resolves the worker package,
install/license rights, runtime profile, authority requirements,
subscription policy, and memory/archive policy. Execution receives a runtime
assignment that selects a daemon-managed or daemon-mediated path. A RuntimeNode
or provider placement may host a local, hosted, DePIN, TEE, customer, or
enterprise environment; GPU jobs, browser sandboxes, containers, and similar
workload classes are resources behind that assignment rather than runtime-node
identities by themselves.

Every execution node that performs IOI work runs, embeds, or speaks to a
daemon-compatible runtime profile. The Daemon decouples logical
isolation from physical hardware via a \textbf{Multi-Plane Scaling
Architecture}. The invariant is: regardless of deployment target, every
admitted path must preserve the declared authority, policy, envelope,
receipt, and Agentgres boundaries. Physical isolation, provider semantics,
capacity, privacy, attestation, and adapter control points vary and must not
be flattened into identical security claims.

Deployment examples: locally (Hypervisor), the planes may collapse into a
user-space virtualization layer over the host OS. On managed IOI or partner
provider infrastructure, they may scale horizontally across four distinct
planes, engaging public settlement only when an explicit trigger requires it:

\textbf{Multi-Plane Scaling Architecture (four logical hosted planes).}

\begin{center}
\needspace{17\baselineskip}
\begin{tikzpicture}[scale=1,transform shape,node distance=6mm and 10mm]
\node[ioiplain,text width=42mm] (client) {\textbf{Client / caller}\\\footnotesize product, API, automation, or adapter};
\node[ioiplain,below=of client,text width=58mm] (a) {\textbf{A. Edge / Admission}\\\footnotesize authenticate, normalize, rate-limit, session admission};
\node[ioibox,below=of a,text width=54mm] (d) {\textbf{D. Daemon / Effect Boundary}\\\footnotesize assignment, policy + authority, effects, receipts};
\node[ioiplain,left=11mm of d,text width=38mm] (b) {\textbf{B. Inference}\\\footnotesize reason and propose; no effect authority};
\node[ioiplain,right=11mm of d,text width=38mm] (c) {\textbf{C. Guest Workload}\\\footnotesize isolated harness, worker, script, or service};
\node[ioiplain,below=of b,text width=38mm] (auth) {\textbf{Authority + Policy}\\\footnotesize grant / deny; D is not the authority owner};
\node[ioibox,below=12mm of d,text width=68mm] (ag) {\textbf{Agentgres}\\\footnotesize admitted operations, state, evidence, replay};
\node[ioiplain,below=of ag,text width=68mm] (l1) {\textbf{Optional external anchor / IOI L1}\\\footnotesize only when enrollment and settlement policy select it};
\draw[ioiflow](client)--(a);
\draw[ioiflow](a)--node[ioilabel,right]{run request}(d);
\draw[ioiflow](d) to[bend right=16] node[ioilabel,below]{model invocation}(b);
\draw[ioiflow](b) to[bend right=16] node[ioilabel,above]{proposal}(d);
\draw[ioiflow](d) to[bend left=16] node[ioilabel,above]{assignment + leases}(c);
\draw[ioiflow](c) to[bend left=16] node[ioilabel,below]{result / effect request}(d);
\draw[ioiflow](auth.east)--node[ioilabel,below,sloped]{decision}(d.south west);
\draw[ioiflow](d)--node[ioilabel,right]{admit + record}(ag);
\draw[-{Stealth[length=3mm]},thick,dashed](ag)--node[ioilabel,right]{selected roots only}(l1);
\end{tikzpicture}
\end{center}

\emph{Planes A--C scale horizontally. Plane D scales only through governed
membership, ordering, admission, and fencing; it is never cloned as a
stateless worker. On a local deployment the logical planes may co-locate on one
machine without collapsing their authority, isolation, or evidence contracts.}

The \textbf{Institutional Learning Boundary} overlays these four planes; it is
not a fifth one. Edge admission carries the applicable boundary revision,
inference routes resolve bidirectional learning rights, guest workloads receive
only policy-bound projections, and the daemon enforces or blocks egress before
Agentgres records the decision and lineage. Foundry later consumes only
individually eligible evidence under the same boundary. Selected public roots
may be anchored externally, but protected learning contents do not move to IOI
L1 merely because their commitments exist.

Plane A: The Edge / Admission Plane

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Role:} The stateless API and routing layer.
\item
  \textbf{Responsibilities:} Handles initial authentication, rate
  limiting, request normalization, routing, and session admission. It
  acts as the programmatic ingress for hosted \emph{ioi.ai} queries and
  third-party dApps.
\end{itemize}

Plane B: The Inference Plane

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Role:} The cognitive engine.
\item
  \textbf{Responsibilities:} Horizontally scaled by model pool and queue
  depth. It handles fast reasoning, embeddings, and rerankers. It
  may utilize \emph{warm} provider or self-hosted capacity where its route
  contract allows. A BYOK/BYOA route declares its credential principal and
  authority profile. Typed wallet.network request/grant binding can support
  brokered custody, but end-to-end key delivery, proxying, and provider
  invocation remain route-specific and require execution evidence.
\end{itemize}

Plane C: The Guest Workload Plane

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Role:} The isolated environment where a model-backed worker,
  external harness, script, service module, or third-party binary
  attempts tool use. It is mediated away from provider-visible secrets,
  host authority, and the user's primary state by daemon policy,
  wallet.network leases, and Agentgres receipts.
\item
  \textbf{Responsibilities:} Horizontally scalable worker nodes that
  execute workflow steps, tool calls, browser/runtime jobs, and generate
  raw artifacts.
\item
  \textbf{Isolation:} Runs through declared execution lanes such as
  containers, namespaces, microVMs, WASM workloads, local tools, remote
  managed bridges, provider-backed environments assigned to sessions/WorkRuns,
  or cTEE/private-workspace paths. It
  boots in a zero-trust state. API calls cross daemon-governed mediation
  points such as adapter bridges, capability proxies, MCP gateways, or
  wallet.network leases, each enforcing the active authority envelope before
  effects are admitted.
\end{itemize}

Plane D: Hypervisor Daemon / Coordinator Plane (The Effect Boundary)

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Role:} The bounded, capacity-governed execution-control role.
  This is the always-on daemon boundary that holds run state, policy
  bundles, tenant configurations, and cryptographic receipts while
  requesting decisions from local/domain policy and the applicable authority
  provider. wallet.network supplies portable delegated and designated
  high-risk authority paths; it is not required for every local act.
\item
  \textbf{Runtime Node Modes:} Execution venues that run Hypervisor
  daemon profiles.

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Hosted IOI Runtime:} Hosted by the provider or
    provider-managed infrastructure for fast, consumer-facing tasks.
  \item
    \emph{Customer VPC Runtime:} Deployed directly inside a
    customer\textquotesingle s VPC or on-prem environment, allowing
    \emph{sas.xyz} to orchestrate tasks without exfiltrating enterprise
    data.
  \item
    \emph{Local Hypervisor:} Embedded inside Hypervisor on the
    user\textquotesingle s personal device.
  \item
    \emph{IOI Authority Gateway (Sidecar Profile):} Run locally or
    within customer boundaries to act as an external execution and
    policy boundary. Rather than serving as the primary interface, it
    runs as a background process ("sidecar") to intercept and normalize
    action requests from third-party cognitive environments, obtain the
    applicable policy and authority decision, and admit, deny, or mediate the
    resulting effect.
  \item
    \emph{Customer Boundary Runtime:} Deployed inside a customer VPC or
    on-prem environment so protected inputs and internal capabilities can remain
    inside the declared boundary while only explicitly declassified outputs,
    evidence, and receipts cross it.
  \item
    \emph{Hardware-Attested Confidential Runtime:} A TEE-backed runtime
    that may provide hardware attestation and memory-confidential
    execution under a vendor-specific threat model. Standard
    confidential VMs do not guarantee absolute protection against a
    compromised physical host. Vendor attestation, measured-boot evidence,
    cTEE, customer custody, and cryptographic operators provide different,
    non-interchangeable claims under their declared threat models. A TEE is
    one admissible private-execution substrate among several.
  \item
    \emph{Cryptographic Operator Runtime:} A proof-carrying runtime that
    uses FHE, MPC, ZK proofs, verifiable computation, or a hybrid
    construction to produce externally verifiable evidence without
    treating hardware attestation as the root of validity.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{wallet.network guardian/access-point profile:} Operating within
  Hypervisor Core or the wallet.network authority path, a guardian/access-point profile
  may hold key shares, device attestations, approval state, or protected
  signing authority for a runtime. It does not by itself define protocol
  validity. Its signatures are accepted only when bound to canonical
  requests, policy hashes, monotonic sequence state, receipt obligations,
  wallet.network authority refs, and the applicable verifier
  requirements. Such a profile may integrate a minimal receipt sequencer
  (remote, local, or enclave-bound depending on the threat model) that
  maintains a persistent, monotonic counter (\emph{seq}) on disk to
  enforce an append-only, non-equivocating receipt chain.
\end{itemize}

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{\linewidth}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
 \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{Safety Invariant:}\emph{\textbf{ }}Because the receipt
sequencer enforces monotonic sequence advancement on disk, equivocation
becomes detectable under the declared storage and runtime threat model.
A compromised host or execution worker cannot produce valid higher-tier
evidence unless it also satisfies the receipt-chain, verifier, and
challenge requirements for that action class. \\
\end{longtable}

\hypertarget{plane-enforced-isolation}{%
\subsubsection{2.2.1 Plane-Enforced
Isolation}\label{plane-enforced-isolation}}

For daemon-controlled workloads and capabilities, Plane C (where cognition
and guest work occur) is separated from Plane D (where the daemon evaluates
policy, requests applicable authority, and commits receipted state). Managed
I/O crosses the daemon effect boundary. Adapter profiles mediate only their
declared control points, so containment and interception claims must name the
actual substrate. When a brokered secret is required, wallet.network or an
approved authority client performs the capability or issues an operation-
scoped lease without exposing ambient secret material to the worker.

\hypertarget{deterministic-io-and-pinned-externalities}{%
\subsubsection{2.2.2 Deterministic IO and Pinned
Externalities}\label{deterministic-io-and-pinned-externalities}}

Pinned I/O is a versioned runtime-profile property, not a claim that IOI
eliminates all nondeterminism or intercepts every opaque external process. A
profile declares which externalities it mediates, how it binds them, and which
claims its receipts support:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Sequencing and time:} Replay-critical policy and authority checks use
  the sequence, expiry, revocation epoch, monotonic source, or trusted time
  source declared by their owner contract. Wall-clock observations may support
  UX and telemetry but do not become settlement truth merely by being logged.
\item
  \textbf{Network and tools:} A mediated call resolves through a
  RuntimeToolContract or surface MCP contract. The request, authority/policy
  decision, response commitment, artifacts, and normalized observation are
  covered by the applicable receipt profile.
\item
  \textbf{Randomness:} Any random selection relied upon for eligibility,
  challenge, routing, or settlement declares its source, bias assumptions,
  commitment/reveal or verifier method, and replay semantics. No universal VRF
  construction is fixed in this synthesis.
\item
  \textbf{UI and physical context:} A computer-use adapter may require
  application/window/DOM/visual target bindings and refuse a mismatch before
  action. The exact focus, freshness, and observation checks belong to the
  adapter contract; an unobserved UI surface is not claimed to be contained.
\end{itemize}

The invariant is coverage honesty: consequential effects crossing a declared
daemon or adapter boundary are canonicalized, gated, and receipted according
to that profile. Nondeterministic cognition, wall time, provider behavior, and
unmediated external state remain outside the proof unless a named evidence
source and verifier cover them.
The ``Run Anywhere'' Property

IOI's portability is achieved by separating kernel semantics from
workload packaging.

The \textbf{Hypervisor Daemon} and the underlying workload/kernel
substrate provide the execution invariant: they define how policies
bind, how receipts are formed, and how attestations are produced.

Workloads are packaged as \textbf{Universal Protocol Artifacts} (e.g.,
OCI images or equivalent bundles), allowing a workflow built locally on
a laptop to run on a cloud provider or committee node without changing its
portable contract. Transportability does not preserve every trust claim:
each environment declares its evidence and verifier profile, and receipts
advance only through the exact assurance ladder \texttt{attested},
\texttt{evidenced}, \texttt{verified}, \texttt{accepted},
\texttt{adjudicated}, and \texttt{settled}. A provider attestation, bond,
certificate, or public commitment may add evidence or recourse, but none
silently upgrades a receipt to a later stage.

\hypertarget{the-sidecar-deployment-profile-ioi-authority-gateway}{%
\subsubsection{2.2.3 The Sidecar Deployment Profile (IOI Authority
Gateway)}\label{the-sidecar-deployment-profile-ioi-authority-gateway}}

When running in sidecar compatibility mode, the \textbf{IOI Authority
Gateway} profile lets the Hypervisor Daemon operate as a deterministic,
policy-enforcing boundary for external, unaligned processes. In this
profile, the daemon does not own the external harness's cognitive loop
(the "thinking"). Instead, it mediates available control points and maps
proposed effects into Hypervisor proposals, gates, observations, and
receipts at host operating system, tool, and network boundaries.

This architecture implements the core thesis: \textbf{Models reason;
local/domain policy and the applicable authority provider authorize power;
the Hypervisor Daemon admits, enforces, and executes action.} wallet.network
is the portable delegated and designated high-risk authority profile, not the
source of every local decision.

A. Control Points and Interception Boundaries

Because external agent harnesses and editor/CLI/browser environments
(such as Cursor, Claude Code, Codex, OpenHands, Aider, DeepSeek-style
TUI harnesses, or proprietary hosted agents) expose only partial control
points, the Authority Gateway mediates the boundaries it can actually
observe through six deterministic control surfaces:

1. \textbf{Shell Commands:} The gateway intercepts terminal executions,
verifying package installations, file deletions, network sockets,
process spawns, and deployment commands against the active daemon policy
bundle.

2. \textbf{File System Watcher:} Monitors workspace diffs and git
configuration files. The gateway blocks unauthorized writes to protected
system directories or sensitive file extensions.

3. \textbf{Git Hook Mediation:} Enforces policies on branches,
force-pushes, and commit signing, automatically binding signed commit
hashes to corresponding execution receipts.

4. \textbf{Secret Isolation (wallet.network):} In a compliant brokered-secret
route, API keys and deployment credentials remain within wallet.network or the
declared authority custodian. Typed request/grant records may authorize the
authority boundary to execute the capability or release operation-scoped
material to an approved target. The current baseline proves request and grant
binding; actual proxy, tool, browser, or provider delivery and non-exposure are
route-specific and require their own execution and receipt evidence.

5. \textbf{Hypervisor MCP Gateway:} Exposes only the tools, surfaces,
sessions, automations, Foundry actions, and receipt/replay views selected by an
expiring or revocable gateway profile. Each call resolves to a declared
\textbf{RuntimeToolContract}, surface MCP contract, or operator-plane contract,
then crosses daemon admission and the applicable wallet.network authority path
before Agentgres records the result. A gateway profile is not a master key,
direct provider-credential broker, host-mutation bypass, or peer runtime.
Packages, application releases, adapters, and System manifests may carry an
immutable \textbf{MCPGatewayRequirementEnvelope}. Admission may satisfy that
requirement through native capabilities, service modules, connectors, or a
concrete gateway profile; MCP-mediated live work receives a separately
admitted, subject-scoped, expiring gateway profile. GoalRunProfiles,
WorkflowTemplates, and SkillManifests remain transport-neutral. MCP tools
normalize to RuntimeToolContracts; resources to policy-bound views, artifacts,
or memory projections under ContextLease; prompts to untrusted import inputs;
elicitation to typed user input with separate authority approval; tasks to
opaque external handles on HarnessInvocation; and Apps to sandboxed
\texttt{extension\_application} surfaces. No MCP session, task, prompt, or
resource identity replaces IOI run, state-root, authority, or receipt truth.

6. \textbf{Context-Aware Approvals:} Requests a wallet.network step-up
approval gate when an external agent attempts an action exceeding
autonomous limits (e.g., spending capital, modifying production
environments).

\hypertarget{goal-kernel-and-typed-step-resolution}{%
\subsubsection{2.2.4 Goal Kernel, Outcome Rooms, and Typed Step
Resolution}\label{goal-kernel-and-typed-step-resolution}}

The \textbf{GoalRunProfile} is the immutable, content-addressed pursuit
specification for a reusable class of goals. It declares the applicable goal and
output contracts, orchestration and constraint-derivation policies, optional
WorkflowTemplate revisions, topology and verifier requirements, skills, harness
and tool requirements, stop/recovery/escalation policy, compatibility, and the
only permitted run-time overrides. A profile is compilable and admission-ready;
it does not execute code, grant authority, select live leases, own artifacts, or
carry domain state.

Hypervisor Core and the daemon resolve one selected profile revision with the
admitted constraints and overrides into a durable \textbf{GoalRun}. Every newly
admitted run, including ad hoc work resolved through the generic-adaptive
profile, freezes the exact profile revision and content hash, admitted override
set reference and hash, effective constraint envelope, resolved-component
snapshot reference and hash, and \textbf{GoalRunProfileResolutionReceipt}. The
\textbf{Goal Kernel} then interprets that frozen resolution, operates a
\textbf{GoalGroundingLoop}, forms and revises
\textbf{OrchestrationPlan} objects, selects or adapts a
\textbf{RoleTopology}, leases only the context and authority each role needs,
and requests compatible workers through daemon-mediated
\textbf{HarnessInvocation} objects,
verifies results, and reconciles
receipts, memory proposals, skills, and continuation state. The Goal Kernel is
orchestration behavior, not the authoritative run creator, a super-agent, a
swarm-control interface, or a runtime beside the daemon.

The reusable composition boundary is deliberately narrow. A
\textbf{WorkflowTemplate} owns optional directed graph shape; an
\textbf{AutomationSpec} binds an exact template revision to standing triggers,
schedules, service entrypoints, or approval behavior; an immutable successor-
versioned \textbf{AutomationInstallationBinding} owns scope enablement and
narrowing overlays; and an \textbf{AutomationRun} freezes all three exact
revisions/hashes for one activation. A \textbf{SkillManifest} supplies
immutable versioned procedure and support material; each \textbf{SkillEntry}
binding revision immutably binds local admission and enablement to one exact
manifest revision while lifecycle remains a registry projection; and
an \textbf{ActiveSkillSetSnapshot} freezes the exact admitted selection for a
run or invocation. Runtime hooks remain separately typed executable machinery,
and agent-callable effects cross a \textbf{RuntimeToolContract}. A
\textbf{HarnessProfile} resolves one assigned scoped step. The enclosing
GoalRun, AutomationRun, WorkRun, Foundry job, or domain object owns live state.
``Recipe'' remains product/package language for an owner-qualified composition,
not a generic canonical envelope.

Editable canvas, document, design, ontology, source-tree, campaign, fleet, and
business state stays with its domain owner. Materialization records the exact
editable-object revision as an immutable source snapshot, then links every
derived export to that snapshot, its tool or WorkflowTemplate revision, run,
and receipt. Export therefore adds source $\rightarrow$ snapshot
$\rightarrow$ derived-artifact lineage; it does not create an ExportHarness or
move artifact ownership into a HarnessProfile.

The Goal Kernel operates at the bounded-run scale. Persistent collective
pursuit sits one level above it in an \textbf{OutcomeRoom}. An OutcomeRoom
is instantiated through the reusable room package and genesis as its own
bounded-DAS system. It binds a durable objective to a
\textbf{CollaborativeWorkGraph}: a governed
frontier of questions, hypotheses, tasks, review needs, verification needs,
resource needs, claims, attempts, findings, verifier challenges, admitted
outcome deltas, contribution lineage, budget, and replay. One room may contain
one or more GoalRuns, and a GoalRun may stand alone. Direct questions,
one-shot runs, ordinary automations, and single sessions do not acquire room
machinery merely because the substrate supports it.


\begin{center}
\needspace{20\baselineskip}
\begin{tikzpicture}[scale=1,transform shape,node distance=5mm and 9mm]
\node[ioibox,text width=92mm] (room) {\textbf{OutcomeRoom (optional durable DAS)}\\\footnotesize shared objective, terms, participant leases, frontier, claims, admission};
\node[ioiplain,below left=8mm and -17mm of room,text width=40mm] (g1) {\textbf{GoalRun A}\\\footnotesize its own bounded Goal Kernel loop};
\node[ioiplain,below right=8mm and -17mm of room,text width=40mm] (g2) {\textbf{GoalRun B..N}\\\footnotesize each has its own bounded loop};
\coordinate (goalruns) at ($(g1.south)!0.5!(g2.south)$);
\node[ioibox,below=8mm of goalruns,text width=92mm] (daemon) {\textbf{Per-GoalRun Goal Kernel pursuit loop}\\\footnotesize orient $\rightarrow$ plan $\rightarrow$ act $\rightarrow$ observe $\rightarrow$ verify\\daemon-mediated HarnessInvocations / workers; repair / continue / close};
\node[ioiplain,below=of daemon,text width=92mm] (result) {\textbf{WorkResult / OutcomeDelta}\\\footnotesize proposed result; never self-admitting};
\node[ioibox,below=of result,text width=92mm] (admit) {\textbf{Verification + declared owner / room admission}\\\footnotesize admit, reject, challenge, or request repair};
\node[ioiplain,below=of admit,text width=58mm] (solo) {\textbf{Standalone GoalRun}\\\footnotesize its own bounded loop; bypasses room machinery};
\draw[ioiflow](room)--node[ioilabel,left]{participant + work-claim leases}(g1);
\draw[ioiflow](room)--node[ioilabel,right]{participant + work-claim leases}(g2);
\draw[ioiflow](g1)--(daemon);
\draw[ioiflow](g2)--(daemon);
\draw[-{Stealth[length=3mm]},thick,dashed](solo.west) -- ++(-6mm,0) |- node[ioilabel,left,pos=0.28]{direct run (no room)}(daemon.west);
\draw[ioiflow](daemon)--(result);
\draw[ioiflow](result)--(admit);
\draw[ioiflow](admit.east) -- ++(6mm,0) |- node[ioilabel,right,pos=0.25]{room frontier update}(room.east);
\end{tikzpicture}
\end{center}

Every consequential room child uses the \textbf{RoomAdmittedObjectBase} proof
spine: exact participant lease or room-system issuer, expected room revision and
predecessor transition commitment, payload/operation commitment, admission
policy and decision, monotonic sequence, admission proof, and resulting
revision, transition commitment, state root, and receipt root. This makes
untrusted local-agent proposals useful without making them trusted room truth.

Every persistent OutcomeRoom declares one shared-state ordering and admission
topology. Under \texttt{hosted\_admission}, one named governed domain orders
and admits room-level frontier, attempt, finding, evaluation, and decision
updates. Under \texttt{federated\_admission}, a versioned policy names the
participating domains, ordering or merge rules, quorum or adjudicator
requirements, conflict behavior, failover, recovery, and policy-version
transitions. Both modes preserve each party's local operational truth and
private context. A board, chat, inbox, digest, leaderboard, or replay is a
projection over admitted objects, never a universal mutable database or
authority source.

Each independent role works in a \textbf{ContextCell}. A
\textbf{ContextLease} bounds files, documentation, memory projections,
tools, connectors, budget, receipts, and authority. A typed
\textbf{ContextHandoff} moves a task brief, bounded result, finding, blocker,
test result, review request, verification result, resource request, decision
request, or continuation summary between cells. This preserves long-horizon
intent while preventing every actor from receiving a global context dump.
Every RoleTopology binding names an accountable actor separately from its
HarnessProfile or AgentHarnessAdapter resolver, model route, and runtime
assignment. ContextCells project one exact topology role; HarnessInvocation
owns the resolver actually invoked. Context leases are issued only to concrete
ContextCells or HarnessInvocations, never to reusable profiles or adapters.

The step-resolution broker boundary is:

\begin{center}
\textbf{TaskBriefPayload} $\rightarrow$ \textbf{HarnessInvocation}
$\rightarrow$ \textbf{HarnessAdapterEvent} $\rightarrow$
\textbf{WorkResult} / \textbf{OutcomeDelta} $\rightarrow$
\textbf{VerifierPath}.
\end{center}

\textbf{WorkResult} is the generic result seam for software, research,
ontology mutation, incident response, service delivery, physical missions,
review, evaluation, and custom work. \textbf{ImplementationResultPayload} is
only the software-implementation profile carrying changed-file, diff, test,
and implementation-summary fields. \textbf{OutcomeDelta} proposes an admitted
change to a frontier item, finding, ontology, state, capability, policy,
routing prior, or service outcome; producing a result never grants that change
admission by itself.
The brief, invocation, events, WorkResult, and OutcomeDelta share one typed
work-subject ref, which may be a GoalRun, AutomationRun, WorkRun, module run,
claim, or attempt. Direct routine work therefore need not manufacture a child
GoalRun. Goal-shaped Automation steps use an exact GoalRunActivationContract to
create or join one, after which that GoalRun owns its own profile resolution.
A HarnessInvocation is bound to that subject; it never becomes a second work
subject. Any resolver-produced WorkResult also freezes the resolved-component
snapshot/hash and admission receipt plus the exact resolver revision/hash, so
replay cannot substitute current Worker, model-route, tool, skill, runtime,
profile, or adapter heads.

These independently owned objects share one typed lifecycle \emph{mechanics}
layer without acquiring one universal business lifecycle. A
\textbf{WorkLifecycleRecordEnvelope} appends either a kind-specific phase
transition or a typed child-reference fact under an exact expected head,
content commitment, object-scoped idempotency key, owner, authority class,
evidence, and receipt lineage. GoalRun, GoalGroundingLoop, WorkRun,
AutomationRun, HarnessInvocation, ContextCell, and external-handle transitions
therefore keep separate legal-edge and authority tables. Attaching a child
updates only the parent's rebuildable index; it does not mutate or take
ownership of the child.

Cancellation is likewise an operation, not a terminal string assignment. An
admitted cancel or revoke edge derives a \textbf{CancellationFanoutPlan} over
active typed children, including drain, fence, lease-revoke, timeout,
compensation, ambiguous-effect reconciliation, and receipt-preservation duties
as applicable. The plan never claims those owner-executed actions completed.
Immutable archive segments and archive-root/head-bound snapshots preserve
phase, child, idempotency, and receipt lineage across compaction. A shared Rust
kernel and daemon-local durable reference store are the target mechanism for
